(Beiping) Two squads of Japanese patrol police, 268 men, departed for Tonghua last night via the Shenhai Railway. Major Ueda led an independent garrison and many infantrymen to Tongliao last night to attack the Volunteers. (28th, Special Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The situation in Tonghua is critical. According to recent reports, those who have occupied the city have detained the Japanese consul and Japanese residents. 260 Japanese police officers are now traveling by car from Shenyang to the area, which is over 140 miles away. (28th, Reuters)

Volunteers 30

Once Occupied Fanjiatun

Withdrew Due to Lack of Supplies from the Rear

(Beiping) A Shenyang dispatch reports that the Volunteers briefly occupied Fanjiatun, 60 li south of Changchun, on the 26th. The South Manchuria Railway was stopped for three hours. They withdrew due to lack of supplies from the rear. They are currently contacting other Volunteer units to plan attacks on areas near Changchun. The 25th Route Army of Volunteers attacked Qingzhuizi Station twice on the 24th and 26th, engaging in fierce battles with the Japanese army. The Japanese army suffered heavy casualties, and the Volunteers suffered over 20 casualties. (28th, Special Dispatch)

Volunteers 31

Sank a Japanese Troop Transport Ship

Forty Japanese Soldiers Drowned

(Harbin) A shallow-water motorboat carrying Japanese soldiers downstream was attacked by Volunteers at Laoshan Tou, east of Harbin, on the 27th. One ship was sunk, and forty Japanese soldiers drowned. The Jiangfang warships Lijiang and Lishui each carried over a hundred Japanese soldiers downstream to Yilan. The sailors on the ships all swam away mid-journey, taking advantage of lax surveillance. The Japanese army has recruited hundreds of White Russian technicians in Harbin to fill the vacancies. (28th, Special Dispatch)

(Harbin) Japanese troopships heading downstream arrived at Tonghe on the 27th and are proceeding very slowly. Ma Zhanshan's 3rd Brigade is cooperating with the Yilan Self-Defense Army from Tangyuan on the north bank of the river. The Japanese troopships are hesitant to advance rashly. There are a total of ten Japanese troopships and twenty-five towed barges heading downstream, along with a hundred sailing boats. There are many straw men tied on the sailing boats, the purpose of which is unclear. The mates, stewards, and sailors on the Japanese troop-carrying sailing ships have all fled mid-journey. The Japanese soldiers have specially assigned shifts to supervise them and prevent them from acting freely. (28th, Special Dispatch)

Ma Zhanshan to Attack Harbin 32

His Cavalry Has Reached Hulan

Significant Activity of Black Army on the Hu-Hai Line

(Harbin) 28th The Harbin businesses opened at 10:00 AM, with rumors that Ma Zhanshan's cavalry had reached Hulan and would attack Harbin. The city is under special alert today. (28th, Special Dispatch)

(Harbin) The Japanese army has taken over the management of train operations on the Harbin-Suifenhe line between Shitouhezi and Yimianpo. All employees of the Chinese Eastern Railway have been dismissed. The cavalry battalion of the Japanese army's Murai Brigade was pushed to Hailin on the 27th, and armored vehicles reached Hengdaohezi. (28th, Special Dispatch)

(Harbin) The Japanese army has transferred over a hundred technical personnel from the South Manchuria Railway to work on the eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway. (28th, Special Dispatch)

(Harbin) Residents in the Zhuhai area of the eastern line have been notified by a certain party to evacuate within a week. The Chinese Eastern Railway will provide special trains to transport them to Harbin free of charge. (28th, Special Dispatch)

(Harbin) News received here today states that the Japanese army occupied Hailin last night. Hailin is located on the eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway, about 200 miles from Harbin. Although the Japanese cavalry has entered the town, the main force of the Japanese army is still at Hengdaohezi, about 30 miles from Hailin, because the railway tracks have been destroyed and they are unable to advance. It is reported that the Japanese military authorities have occupied about fifty miles of the Chinese Eastern Railway from Shitouhezi to Hengdaohezi. Further news from the front line indicates that the anti-Manchukuo forces have an armored train manned by Russians who are firing artillery. However, it is not known whether these Russians are Bolsheviks or White Russians. Banditry in eastern Northern Manchuria remains intense. Recently, bandits demanded 20,000 yuan from the Railway Bureau but were unsuccessful. They then attacked the forestry area operated by the Chinese Eastern Railway near Shitouhezi. Several Russians were injured, timber was burned, and all horses were looted. (27th, Reuters)

(Harbin) At 11:40 this morning, approximately 1,500 Volunteers attacked the Hu-Hai Railway and have occupied the entire line. (28th, Domei News Agency)

(Tokyo) A telegram from Harbin states that the Black Army on the Hulan to Hailin line and the Keshan to Qiqihar line is once again very active. The Hulan-Hailin route was cut off last night. In Songpu (transliteration), across from Harbin, ten locomotives and one hundred and twenty train cars have been seized by the Black Army. Therefore, the Japanese army has rushed to the area to maintain order. (28th, Reuters)

(Harbin) The brigade under Murai has reached Hailin on the eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway. Yoda's infantry and artillery units will arrive at Yimianpo. As of now, they have apparently not yet come into contact with anti-Manchukuo forces. It is reported that there are 2,000 guerrillas gathered in Fuyu on the southern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway, and another 7,000 are scattered throughout the surrounding area. (28th, Reuters)

Puppet State Police Claim 33

Clues in Bridge Bombing Case

Believe it's Connected to the Communist Party

Japanese Authorities Not Giving it Much Importance

(Harbin) According to the police of the "Manchukuo", the bombing of the Songhua River bridge was carried out by the Soviet Russian Communist Party. Important clues have now been found, so the perpetrators of the incident involving the Japanese troop train on April 12th will not be difficult to track down. Documents seized have revealed a plot to destroy the bridges over the Songhua River and Nen River, which was allegedly masterminded by the Soviet Russian authorities. Several well-known financiers, consular officials, and Soviet Russian merchants in northern Manchuria are involved in the case. The Communist Party has provided spiritual and financial support to this violent organization, which has 2,978 members. Its leader is Gaituk, the secretary of the General Affairs Department of the Chinese Eastern Railway. Most of the members have received training from military authorities in Khabarovsk. They came to Harbin between October and November of last year. Those who join the organization must swear an oath that they will not hesitate to kill even their parents if ordered to do so. Those who violate orders or leak secrets of the organization will be sentenced to death. The explosives needed were all transported from Blagoveshchensk. (28th, Reuters)

(Tokyo) Commenting today on the Manchurian government's accusation of a Soviet Russian plot to disrupt Manchurian security, a Foreign Ministry spokesperson said that even if Japanese officials confirm that the bombing of the Japanese troop train was a Communist plot, relations between Russia and Japan will not necessarily become strained as a result. This is because it is believed that the case is only the action of individuals. The military also seems to hold the same opinion. According to the Jiji Shimpo, Army Minister Araki said that if it is determined that Chinese Eastern Railway officials are involved in the case, the Japanese government may lodge a protest with Soviet Russia, but he believes that there will be no serious consequences. (28th, Reuters)

It was resolved to approve the case, and to send another telegram to Chairman Ma and Commander Ma of the Ningxia provincial government to investigate and report. (4) The Secretariat of the National Crisis Conference sent a letter containing the first batch of resolutions of the National Crisis Conference, including three on diplomacy, nine on internal affairs, sixteen on military affairs, one on finance, one on judicial affairs, and two on Mongolian and Tibetan affairs, requesting adoption and implementation. Important Foreign Telegrams

Tardieu Claims Illness 79

Suspends Trip to Geneva

Evades Joint Pressure from Britain and America

Conference of Five Major Powers Fails

Franco-German Compromise Dissolves

Stimson Deeply Disappointed

Will Return to America Via Italy

A Certain British Official Issues a Warning

Stating that Ship-Building Plans Will Be Resumed

Special Telegram from the National News Agency in Geneva on the 27th: Today, French representative, Peng Gu, informed U.S. Secretary of State Stimson and British Prime Minister MacDonald that French Premier Tardieu would be unable to come to Geneva on Friday due to illness. Consequently, the highly anticipated conference of the five major powers will be canceled, and all hopes for a Franco-German compromise will be dashed. Stimson and MacDonald have repeatedly stated that European countries can contribute more during this period than any other nation. British and American navies are already limited, and their armies can be considered practically at a minimum. Therefore, the adherence of Italy and France to the London Naval Treaty and a Franco-German compromise are considered the most urgent matters.

Special Telegram from the National News Agency in Geneva on the 27th: It is believed here that French Premier Tardieu's excuse of illness to suspend his trip to Geneva indicates his unwillingness to change his attitude towards disarmament, reparations, and Germany. He seeks to evade discussions in Geneva to avoid pressure from Britain and America. It is said that Stimson and MacDonald planned to exert some pressure on Tardieu to ensure French support for the Anglo-American theory of qualitative disarmament. If France supports this, the disarmament conference is expected to achieve some success. This would raise hopes for the United States to make some concessions on the war debt issue. Now, with the French Premier's suspension of his trip to Geneva, talks between leaders of major powers have also been suspended, and all hopes have vanished. Unexpectedly, Segrant also informed this place that he would remain in Rome and suspend his trip to Geneva. The U.S. Secretary of State will depart for Italy tomorrow and take the Italian liner "Roma" from Genoa to New York on Friday. The fact that Stimson is returning home via Italy instead of France is considered highly significant. According to reliable sources, Stimson is deeply disappointed with the course of events. This situation is sufficient to negate all hopes of American concessions on war debts. British Prime Minister MacDonald and German Chancellor Brüning will also depart for home tomorrow. After returning home, the German Chancellor will face a critical situation, as France's attitude will further increase the power of the National Socialist Party.

Special Telegram from the National News Agency in Geneva on the 28th: U.S. Secretary of State Stimson has firmly decided to travel by car to Cannes after lunch on Saturday and return home in a few days.

Special Telegram from the National News Agency in Berlin on the 28th: German Chancellor Brüning will return to Berlin tonight. Tomorrow morning, he will visit the President to report on the Geneva consultations. Immediately afterwards, a special cabinet meeting will be held to discuss the situation after the failure of the five-power conference.

Special Telegram from the National News Agency in Paris on the 27th: The political circles were shocked tonight after the announcement that French Premier Tardieu had canceled his trip to Geneva and suspended his election speech in Belfort. According to official announcements, Tardieu is suffering from laryngitis due to overwork, and doctors strongly advise rest. Even if he went to Geneva, he would not be able to participate in the meetings of British, American, Italian, and German officials. Therefore, it had to be temporarily canceled. It was strongly denied that Tardieu's illness had diplomatic implications, and it was stated that it was due to overwork from simultaneously handling national affairs, directing the election campaign, and attending the Geneva conference.

Reuters Telegram from Paris on the 27th: French Premier Tardieu is unable to go out due to laryngitis. He has now received a telegram from U.S. Secretary of State Stimson stating that he is saddened that the important matters recently considered in Geneva cannot be reconvened. He cannot stay in Geneva for long due to health reasons, but the U.S. delegation in Geneva will do its utmost to promote the spirit of this discussion to the extent of its power. Negotiations between France and Italy on naval issues have been delayed for months without resolution. Reuters Telegram from London on the 27th: A Geneva telegram states that a certain important British politician stated to journalists there that Britain believes that the progress of disarmament discussions is too slow and disappointing. He also stated that Britain may have to consider using the articles of the London Naval Treaty that allow the building of warships within specified limits. French Premier Tardieu is not currently in Geneva, as he is suffering from laryngitis and must rest. It is generally believed that this forced rest is not necessarily a bad thing, as it can avoid open frustration in Geneva. Tardieu is currently living an extremely busy life, not only having to conduct extremely important diplomatic negotiations in Paris and Geneva, but also having to conduct an election campaign in his electoral district of Belfort. Tardieu recently stayed in his electoral district for sixty hours, spending forty-five hours speaking at open-air rallies. Tardieu now has a good chance of being re-elected, and although he is temporarily ill, he can still direct the campaign from his Paris residence. However, the fact that Tardieu was unable to meet as scheduled with British Prime Minister MacDonald and U.S. Secretary of State Stimson in Geneva on Friday may have far-reaching consequences, as the mediation of the British and American prime ministers between the opinions of Tardieu and German Chancellor Brüning has been at least temporarily shelved. Stimson cannot wait long in Geneva and is scheduled to return to the United States via the Riviera on Friday, while MacDonald cannot stay long in Geneva either. Since the election victory of Nazi leader Hitler in Germany, France has decided not to make any further concessions to Germany. Therefore, it is doubtful whether there can be any genuine understanding between Tardieu and Brüning.

Special Telegram from the National News Agency in Berlin on the 28th: Yesterday evening, German political circles were deeply disappointed upon hearing the news that the five-power conference scheduled to be held in Geneva tomorrow had been canceled. This morning, almost all German newspapers stated that the French Premier's claim of illness was merely an excuse. Editorial comments criticized France for resorting to the same old trick of obstructing the Hoover moratorium on war debt payments last year, and this time secretly undermining hopes of restoring international equilibrium. Conservative newspapers believe that France's failure to support U.S. Secretary of State Stimson's efforts shows the stubbornness of France's attitude, which should make other states, especially Germany, deeply convinced that it is futile to seek understanding with France. It is said that France is determined to scourge Europe and gouge out a pound of flesh from the heart, and nothing can change its determination. Even the more moderate newspapers believe that this five-power conference was a good opportunity to negotiate important resolutions, but France's secret obstruction is truly disappointing. For example, the "Berliner Tageblatt" doubts whether there will be such a good opportunity again in the near future and deeply regrets missing it. It also stated that France's actions will inevitably make the German people more determined to resist France. The "Berliner Mittagspost" stated that this morning's French newspapers did not write a word expressing regret over the cancellation of the five-power conference, which further shows that Tardieu was unwilling to go to Geneva, and his claim of illness was just an excuse. It also stated that political circles in London expressed the deepest regret over the interruption of the talks between the authorities of various countries, believing that the reason was mainly due to the domestic situation and general elections in France. However, the method of interruption was unfortunate, and it is hoped that negotiations can continue after the French elections are completed, but Stimson will not be able to participate in person at that time. Rumors that France is strongly advocating postponing the Lausanne Conference have been proven inaccurate by officials today, stating that Britain knows that the reparations issue needs to be resolved and will never allow it to be postponed.

Hoover Urges Frugality in Government Spending 85

Reuters Telegram from Ridge Manor on the 27th: President Hoover today addressed the Conference of Governors, urging state and local governments to be frugal in government spending. He stated that American expenditures were $2,900,000,000 in 1913 and increased to $13,200,000,000 in 1930. Of this, state and local government expenditures accounted for $9,800,000,000. During this decade and more, government spending as a percentage of national income rose from 8% to 20%, and the amount of debt owed rose from $4,800,000,000 to $30,600,000,000. So much of the nation's private income is consumed by government spending. If this continues, economic soundness will not be restored, as weakening the wealth of the people will stagnate production and consumption, and unemployment will not be reduced.

Public Telegrams

Telegram from Jingjiang: The Shanghai Shenbao Newspaper Office forwards to the charitable organizations and to Zhu Ziqiao, Xu Jingren, Yu Qiaqing, Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yiting, Huang Jinrong, Zhang Xiaolin, Wen Lantin, Zhang Qianmiao and other philanthropists. We are deeply aware that Jingjiang is a small county with a large population, poor land, and impoverished people. The hardships of life are rarely seen in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Moreover, military conflicts and banditry have caused years of famine. In addition, there was a flood last autumn. Because Jingjiang is located on the Yangtze River, many counties in the lower reaches of the river drained through this county, making it difficult for the water to flow away quickly, resulting in the entire area becoming a swamp. The Daoshiguan area of Gushan District was the lowest-lying area in the entire county, known as the "bottom of the pot." The suffering last autumn was the same as that in Xinghua, Yancheng, Gaoyou and Shaobo. Fortunately, the Jiangsu Relief Association distributed some winter relief, which was barely enough to survive the year. However, since the beginning of spring, everything has been eaten and used up. At this time of year when the old harvest is gone and the new harvest is not yet in, the whole county is selling everything, and pawnshops have already announced that they will no longer accept pledges. The disaster victims have no way to borrow, and they are about to become starving corpses. Hungry cries are everywhere, and they are waiting to be fed. Snails and wild vegetables have all been searched and eaten. They are emaciated and many are starving to death, even selling their children and pawning their wives, entrusting orphans and seeking death. Scenes of devastation are unbearable to witness. Furthermore, because the water in the disaster area receded slowly last autumn, wheat seeds could not be planted. In the blink of an eye, the rice planting season is approaching. If relief is not sought quickly, the autumn harvest will likely be disappointing, and the future will be even more unthinkable. Therefore, we dare to plead on behalf of all the disaster victims in the county, asking the great philanthropists to have compassion for the hungry and drowning, to embrace the sick and treat them, and to provide prompt relief to those in distress. Whether it is money or flour, the more the better. We urgently telegraph and hope for relief, and we are extremely eager and hopeful. Liu Zaiji, Chairman of the Jingjiang County Chamber of Commerce; Zhu Xianying, Huang Shaochang, Zheng Xiangzhi, Sun Jiayuan, Standing Committee Members; Zhu Xianying, Zhang Nianhe, Sheng Zhongyan, Guo Jinwen, Zheng Jinzhang, Wang Dayi, Sheng Zhuoqun, Principals of the Red Swastika Society.

Important News

League of Nations 87

Investigation Team Arrives in Shenyang

Investigation Procedures Also Finalized

Shenyang Dispatch: The League of Nations Investigation Team arrived in Dalian on the 21st morning. At 12:50 PM that day, Sir Lytton, Representative Gu Weijun, and their party, along with General Claudel, Dr. Hines, and Liu Chongjie, gathered at the South Manchuria Railway Station. They then headed north to Shenyang. Along the way, many people held flags to welcome them. The special train then slowly departed.

The special train consisted of eleven cars, similar in structure to our country's Jinpu special train. The last car was an observation car. The three commissioners from England, France, and Germany, along with their attendants, occupied one car. Next, the Japanese delegation occupied two cars, followed by the Chinese delegation in one car. It was the seventh in the sequence. Because they were traveling during the day, the cars were not sleeping cars. Sir Lytton, General Claudel, Dr. Hines, Representative Gu Weijun, and Representative Yoshida each occupied two rooms. The rest occupied one room each. However, the personnel of the Chinese delegation had two people per room. When asked, the Japanese delegation said they heard that there were only nine people in the Chinese delegation, not the twenty-odd people reported. The fourth car was occupied by representatives of the Kwantung Government and Japanese reporters. The third car was occupied by personnel of the South Manchuria Railway Company. The remaining cars were dining cars and baggage cars. Along the way, soldiers and police were stationed, creating tight security.

Around 2 PM, the train passed Pulandian. Rumors spread that the puppet Manchukuo would arrest the representatives of the Gu delegation, but nothing happened. The stations of San Shili Pu, Wafangdian, Dashiqiao, Anshan, and Liaoyang were stopped at briefly, either to add coal and water or to give way to southbound trains. The roadside was adorned with English slogans from the puppet Manchukuo. One depicted a dove with the words "Welcome Peace Envoy," and another said, "Join hands to build Manchukuo, the Geneva of the East." At Liaoyang Station, a military band and people holding five-colored flags lined up to welcome the delegation. The members of the investigation team did not get off the train, as it was dinnertime.

At 8:30 PM, the train arrived in Shenyang, where many people still welcomed them. When exiting the station, reporters from the Japanese Shinpo newspaper took the opportunity to take photographs, with magnesium flashes booming like a string of firecrackers. After arriving at the Yamato Hotel, five young women presented flowers to the investigation team. However, Sir Lytton had not yet recovered his health and was represented by his personal secretary, Mr. Easton. Rooms 201 to 208 of the Yamato Hotel were reserved for the Chinese delegation, with Representative Gu residing in Room 201. The others were accommodated in the Far East Hotel.

The party of Earl Lytton's land-based group, Major General McCoy, and Dr. Haas, after arriving, said that after departing from Qinhuangdao, they arrived at Shanhaiguan at 11 AM on the 20th. They visited the pass. The special train prepared by the Japanese arrived at 7 PM. Because it was decided to travel during the day, they all stayed in the train. On the 21st at 5:50 PM, they arrived at Jinzhou and got off the train to inspect. On the 22nd, they stopped briefly at the Daling River, arriving in Shenyang half an hour before Sir Lytton and company. This was because Sir Lytton was slightly unwell, causing delays along the way.

The investigation schedule is as follows: four days in Shenyang, departing Shenyang on the 25th evening, passing through Changchun, arriving in Jilin on the 26th morning, returning to Changchun in the afternoon, staying for two days, departing at 10 PM on the 28th for Harbin, arriving on the 29th early morning, staying for five days, going to Qiqihar on May 4th, staying for two days, returning to Shenyang via Sipingjie on the 6th, staying for another six days, visiting the Fushun Coal Mine, visiting the Anshan Iron Mine on the 13th, and returning to Dalian, staying for five days, concluding on the 18th. It is currently unknown whether the Chinese representatives will accompany the mission north of Changchun. The personnel of this delegation were each given a metal badge by the South Manchuria Railway Company, with the words "League of Nations" and a miniature of the East Pagoda printed on it, and a train pass, valid from April 20th to May 19th. (April 22nd)

Japanese Army in East Manchuria 88

Withdraws from the Eastern Front

Due to Spring Season Being Unfavorable for Japanese Military Operations

The Volunteer Army Enjoys Natural Advantages

The "China Press" of April 18th reports from Harbin that opinions in Harbin are divided regarding the reason for the Japanese army's withdrawal from the eastern front. Furthermore, there is a lack of understanding as to why the Japanese troops along that route are being dispatched to Changchun on a daily basis. Not long ago, the commanders of various brigades heading towards the northeast of Harbin informed reporters from Russian newspapers in Harbin that their work had been completely completed. All bandits and government forces had been driven outside the line extending from Fangzheng in the west to Wujimishi in the east. Therefore, there was no need for the Japanese army to pursue them further. However, since the Japanese army's withdrawal from the aforementioned line, the former Jilin troops have returned and occupied many of the outermost stations along the Chinese Eastern Railway outside the city. Now they have even reached the right bank of the Songhua River. In reality, the Japanese army's withdrawal is due to the fact that it is currently spring, and the roads are soft and slippery, making it inconvenient for automobiles to travel. Infantry and artillery units are also unable to pass, making it very difficult to deal with guerrilla warfare. Furthermore, in another week, the rivers of northern Manchuria will begin to thaw, and troops will no longer be able to cross the rivers as they did in winter. Therefore, the Chinese army will enjoy various natural advantages. If, during this period of dormancy, the Chinese army receives a supply of ammunition, it will be extremely difficult to drive them from their current positions. There are widespread rumors that the various towns have been greatly devastated since the withdrawal of the Japanese army from the eastern front. However, according to people who have arrived in Harbin from that area in recent days, this is not the case. Even if there is banditry, it is nothing more than what is commonly seen every spring. (Translator's note: Recent foreign dispatches frequently report various news about banditry on the Chinese Eastern Railway, indicating that it is all propaganda.) The easternmost section of the Chinese Eastern Railway still flies the old "Blue Sky, White Sun, and Red Earth" flag, as the former Jilin troops do not allow the stationmasters to replace it with the new flag of the puppet state. At present, the matter of greatest attention is the upcoming arrival of the League of Nations Investigation Team. The Japanese will do their utmost to prove that they are working for the welfare of the people, rather than being hostile to them. However, the Chinese people of all of Manchuria are still strongly opposed to Japan's occupation of their land by force, and they have no trust in the government of Manchukuo, which is completely controlled by Japanese soldiers. Generally, observers of the current situation believe that it is inevitable that the Japanese army will declare war on Soviet Russia. However, although Soviet Russia has fully prepared for war, it seems to have no intention of engaging in combat.

Recently, a large Russian army has moved eastward again, making the problem quite serious. Therefore, one cannot be at ease regarding the situation in Manchuria. Hence (Hashimoto) feels that the situation is tense and the responsibility is great due to his rapid appointment.

Situation After the Fall of Zhangzhou 92

Factories and Shops Confiscated by Bandits

Zhang's Division and Yang's Brigade Completely Routed

Situation in Quanzhou and Xiamen Becomes Increasingly Critical

Fuzhou Dispatch: The Red bandits in western Fujian have captured Liancheng, Yanping, Nan'an, Longxi (i.e., Zhangzhou). It is reported that the force consists of four units under Luo Binghui, Peng Dehuai, Ji Zhendong, and Lin Biao, totaling over 40,000 men. They are currently stationed outside the city, with only a small number of political workers stationed inside the city. Because no fighting occurred in Zhangzhou City, Zhang's division retreated immediately, so there was no major loss. Inside and outside the city, there are Mao Zedong's public notices to reassure the people, urging businesses and industries to operate as usual. Personnel are sent to investigate the names of shop owners and factory owners of large shops and factories. Generally, bosses, fearing arrest, all pretend to be shop assistants and workers. The party believes that since the capitalists have fled, the factories and shops should be taken over by the public, and workers are allowed to continue working and given pay raises according to their ranks. Personnel dispatched by the puppet government keep accounts in the shops, and the revenue, after deducting expenses, is all turned over for military expenses. The people are strictly forbidden from leaving the country privately. The original military plan was to divide into two routes, one entering Haicheng to pursue Zhang Zhen's division, and the other going out to Tong'an to attack Quanzhou. Later, it was learned that the two divisions of the Guangdong army, Huang Renhuan and Huang Zhiwen, had advanced from Jiaoling and Dapu, respectively, to attack Shanghang and Yongding at the same time, fearing loss of the rear and attack from both sides. Therefore, most of the bandits were transferred to resist in the Nanjian and Longyan areas. Temporarily taking a defensive posture towards Haicheng and Tong'an, Haicheng was occupied by Wu Ci, a bandit from Zhangzhou, the day before yesterday. Zhang's division, Yang Fengnian's brigade, was completely routed, leaving only Wang Zuqing's brigade of about 2,000 men. Zhang himself is now in Yunxiao, arranging defenses. Personnel from various Tong'an agencies also fled. Currently, the provincial defense army Chen Guohui's brigade is strictly blocking the scattered bandits in the area bordering Tong'an and Quanzhou. Quanzhou City has been affected, and business has completely stopped. In Xiamen, there are too many refugees fleeing from Zhangzhou, and there is a shortage of space. Furthermore, it is an island, isolated in the sea. Rice, firewood, and water have always relied on supplies from Longxi, Haicheng, and Tong'an. Now that they are cut off, it is also deeply felt that the situation is difficult. (April 26th)

Ministry of Education 93

Compiles the "Chinese Education Yearbook"

Our country has never had many yearbooks. There has never been an educational yearbook. To meet this need, the Ministry of Education has ordered the first "Chinese Education Yearbook" to be compiled, which will compile and organize important educational facts from the past and recently in our country into a huge book to be distributed to the people. It has been reported that it has been assigned to the Director of the Editorial and Review Office, Xin Shuzhi, Directors Zhang Xiu, Guo Xin, Gu Shusen, Li Zheng, Counselors Yang Fang, Chen Shizhen, Chen Panzao, Wu Chu, Secretary Zhou Gan, Section Chiefs Zhang Fanjiu, Xie Shuying, Guo Youshou, Dai Yingguan, Wu Yan Yin, Zhong Lingxiu, Peng Baichuan, and Wang Ruichang, a total of eighteen people, to form an editorial and review committee to preside over the editorial and review work. It also appointed Zhou Shuxian, Wang Fengtong, Gong Zhengtao, Ke Shuping, Qian Wangzhuo, Gao Weichang, Cai Yuyi, Wu Yonglong, Huang Longxian, Zhang Weigao, Huang Wenqi, Wang Wanzhong, Weng Zhida, Chen Zhe, Xue Tianhan, Gu Liangjie, Guo Lianfeng, Jin Guisun, Shu Chushi, Gao Hongtu, He Bolie, Xue Quanzeng, Zhou Bangdao, Hu Yanli, Li Yiyan, Zhou Qixun, Huang Shouzhong, Ding Zhipin and other twenty-eight people to compile. Zhou Bangdao serves as the Chief Compiler. The entire book is divided into five parts: Part A: General Overview of Education; Part B: Education Laws and Regulations; Part C: Overview of Education; Part D: Education Statistics; Part E: Education Miscellany. Each part is divided into chapters and sections, with an estimated total of over six million words. It is scheduled to collect manuscripts by the end of August, edit them in September, review them in October, and send them to print in November. To ensure the accuracy of educational facts, a variety of outline summaries and investigation forms will be printed and circulated to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, universities, and vocational schools for completion and submission by the end of June.

Zhejiang Province's Financial Relief Measures 94

Hangzhou Dispatch: Lu Dipin, the Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, previously telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to discuss measures to deal with the financial difficulties in Zhejiang Province, where the provincial treasury was empty, and cash flow was insufficient. The following requests were made: (1) Regarding previous arrears, it was requested that they be allocated and paid in full as soon as possible; (2) Monthly subsidies of 150,000 yuan were requested to be allocated and distributed nearby by designating the Zhejiang Provincial National Tax Agency; (3) Under the salt tax, the Liangzhe Salt Affairs Audit Sub-Bureau was requested to allocate the full amount monthly according to the collected amount in the future; (4) The liquor and tobacco license tax should be 90% for the province according to the Business Tax Law. The tax funds are requested to be assigned to the province for management, so as to find ways to rectify and increase income. The 10% that should be transferred to the Central Government should still be transferred in full; (5) The income of the Zhejiang Province Sand Reclamation Bureau should be allocated to the province's water conservancy funds. It is requested that the example of Jiangsu Province be followed, and the bureau be assigned to the province for management, with all measures handled in accordance with the established case of Jiangsu Province. The above points are of great importance to the finances of Zhejiang Province. Recently, Finance Minister Song Ziwen visited Hangzhou from Shanghai and summoned Chairman Lu and Director Zhou, etc., to discuss them one by one. It is said that concrete measures have already been reached. (April 28th)

Local News 95

Cruel Abuse of a Female Servant Nantao Dispatch, Cai Xiang, the son of a wealthy man, Yu Yongjie, is a doctor with a lustful nature. He seduced the female servant Ni Yin Nan and got her pregnant. On the 30th, Zhu and others became even more ferocious, dragging Yin Nan from the upstairs to the downstairs wall, calling outsiders to watch. Rampant Local Bandits in the Northeast of the Township Wuxi Dispatch, The northeastern part of Wuxi Township has long been an area where communists gather. After military and police cooperation, the momentum has subsided slightly. However, the remnants are not cleared, and they often make trouble. Recently, they have revived. There are often cases of robbery and ransom. The following is a description: (1) The family of Hu Xiaogui, a resident of Gu Jia Ba in the 11th district, is not wealthy, but five bandits suddenly came to Hu's house the night before last, each holding a handgun and rattan cane, and ordered them to pay 300 yuan. As a result, they collected 60 yuan and agreed to send the rest to a certain family ancestral hall in Baitan Mountain. The bandits then left swaggeringly. (2) The families of Fang Gengbao and Fang Yonggen, villagers in Fangjiaxiang in the district, were invaded by more than 20 bandits the other night, who kidnapped Gengbao and Yonggen and forced their families to prepare 200 yuan in cash each to redeem them in Baitan Mountain. As a result, the two men each raised 100 yuan and sent them there before being released. There are still 200 yuan missing, and they agreed to send it within five days. If they break the agreement, they will burn the Fang family's house.

A Woman from Jiangbei Attempts to Murder Her Husband Wuxi Dispatch, Yang Liansheng, a Jiangbei resident living at No. 122 Dongxin Road, opposite the Yayan Elementary School outside Guangfu Gate in this county, is 31 years old and has been working in Wuxi with his wife, Zhou, for many years. He used to work as a waiter in Rixin Pool. Recently, the bathhouse suddenly closed, so Yang went to Lequan Bathhouse as a replacement. The night before last, after finishing his work and returning home, he asked his wife, Zhou, to buy a bowl of noodles to satisfy his hunger. Unexpectedly, when he ate half a bowl, he suddenly found a lot of mercury in the noodles. Liansheng was shocked and lost consciousness. When the neighbors learned about it, they immediately sent Yang to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. Doctor Zhu made every effort to give him an enema, and he was saved. At the same time, he reported to the Second Sub-Bureau of the Public Security Bureau of the town for investigation. After receiving the report, Sub-Bureau Chief Zhu immediately sent bureau member Liu Qingtai to investigate Yang's home. A small piece of newspaper was found on the ground next to the stove, with mercury residue on it. Zhou was taken to the bureau and transferred to the county court for interrogation. A Traitor Was Captured on Longfeng Mountain A traitor was captured by the garrison on Longfeng Mountain outside the east of Jiangyin the other day. He was from Sidunzi in Jingjiang. He was immediately taken to the regimental headquarters for questioning. He confessed that he had been used by the enemy and received 60 yuan. There were three people who came with him, and two of them had mixed into the city. He had three Japanese one-sen copper coins and one Japanese yen on him. The traitor is now detained in the regimental headquarters, waiting to be dealt with.

Reaction to the Market Strike in Xinfengzhen Zhou Zhipeng, the captain of the Second Patrol of Jiaxing Water Police, accompanied by Zhu Xincan and Xing Huaican, went to Wu Yanqing's house in Xinfengzhen at the beginning of the month to arrest smokers without orders. Because they were all wearing plain clothes and did not show official documents, the town mistakenly thought it was a robbery and spontaneously went on strike. The local security corps also lined up for defense. Various legal groups also telegraphed the provincial government, the county government, and the water police district department. The next day, the district department sent personnel to the town to mediate and persuade the merchants to open their businesses. The matter seemed to have come to an end. Unexpectedly, the county government suddenly received an order from the water police bureau the day before yesterday to send the case to the court for investigation and charged Wu Yanqing and Shen Peiying (head of the security corps) with crimes such as privately smoking opium and obstructing official duties. The court has now issued summonses for investigation on schedule.

The Qian Industry Postpones Opening Zhenjiang Dispatch, The local qian industry was originally scheduled to open on April 25th, but due to the hasty preparations and the incomplete procedures of several companies, it was temporarily announced that the opening would be postponed to May 1st. It is reported that the opening this time is entirely for the purpose of rectifying arrears. New lending operations will not begin until after May 15th. According to insiders, the debts owed by various firms to the qian industry are due to the sealing of Japanese goods and the stranding of capital. Unless there is a solution to the Japanese goods issue and the proceeds from the sale of goods are obtained, it will be impossible to repay them. Various merchants learned of the above news and decided to postpone the listing in order to further determine the method of debt collection during the postponement period. It is reported that only Jin Yuan, Jin Sheng, Yuan Kang, Chang Kang, Zhengtai, Tongyu, Hengxiang and other seven companies are confident of listing. The future of business cannot be reversed.

A Robbery Case in Qishuzhen is Cracked Yangzhou Dispatch, The case of the looting in Qishu Temple Town a few days ago, in which the firearms of the police team were confiscated, has been investigated by the county police team repeatedly. It has now been discovered that the bandits' nest is located in Yanghe, near Hantang Township in the Seventh District. Yesterday, the police team stationed in Yiling Town, together with the security corps of the district, went to encircle and suppress them. A bandit boat was immediately found, and seven rifles and one box cannon confiscated from the Qishu Town police team, as well as twelve box cannon pistols owned by the bandits and other stolen goods, were seized.
